<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f4d9e839-de16-4f80-846e-b7fa3a9dfa2c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_1677257787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677257787" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1677257787?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1677257787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4442778146734426092"><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>One thing I have to admit about the ocean: it's very quiet down there. I mean, really. No more shrieking gulls, crashing of waves, shouts from the surfers. No, under the sea, it's just you and the water and the ghosts who are trying to kill you.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Okay, yeah, so. I wasn't supposed to read this (I am TRYING to save them, but oh boy it isn't working out) but when the holiday weekend is busy and you're doing amazing things like, say, cleaning out all your old clothes so your bedroom closet</span>
  <span id="freeText4442778146734426092" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>One thing I have to admit about the ocean: it's very quiet down there. I mean, really. No more shrieking gulls, crashing of waves, shouts from the surfers. No, under the sea, it's just you and the water and the ghosts who are trying to kill you.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Okay, yeah, so. I wasn't supposed to read this (I am TRYING to save them, but oh boy it isn't working out) but when the holiday weekend is busy and you're doing amazing things like, say, cleaning out all your old clothes so your bedroom closet ceases to be a nightmare, it bodes well to read <b>a book that makes you giddy and that feels like coming home</b>. So, I'm not going to write a long-winded review because we all know I ADORE Jesse and Suze cracks me up. So here are some quotes that I loved from this story...<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Gina let out a horrified shriek, threw back the comforter, and dove to the floor, trying to salvage what she could. I, meanwhile, threw Jesse a very dirty look. <br>But all he said was, "Don't look at me like that, Susannah. You heard what she said about him." He sounded wounded. "She called him ugly."<br>I growled, "<i>I</i> say he's ugly all the time, and you don't ever do that to <i>me.</i>"<br>He lifted the eyebrow with the scar in it, and then said, "Well, it's different when you say it."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Let him go," I said, twisting the tiny hairs hard. This method of torture, I'd discovered recently, was much more effective than my former technique of punching Dopey in the gut. He had, over the past few weeks, greatly built up the muscles in his abdomen wall, undoubtedly as a defense against just this sort of occasion.<br>The only way he could keep me from grabbing him by the short hairs, however, was to shave his head, and this had apparently not occurred to him. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>This was very exciting. I'd never had two boys get into a fight over me before. The fact that one of the boys was my stepbrother, however, and held about as much romantic appeal for me as Max, the family dog, somewhat dampened my enthusiasm. <br>And Michael wasn't much of a catch, either, when you actually thought about it, being a potential murderer, and all.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br>Seriously, I could go on and on and on about how much I love this series and just how happy it makes me...but then what would I have left to say when my favorite book shows up (COUGH book 5 COUGH). Running out of words before the pique of the series...We can't have that now can we?<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<span id="freeTextContainer11278671445210003549">This one perhaps had a more somber mood than the others. Less wacky and more oh, shit things are getting serious.<br/><br/>I love meeting Suze’s best friend, Gina who seems very cool and distinctive.   <span id="freeText11278671445210003549" style="display:none">This one perhaps had a more somber mood than the others. Less wacky and more oh, shit things are getting serious.<br /><br />I love meeting Suze’s best friend, Gina who seems very cool and distinctive. I seriously love how the characters in this series are so relatable and fleshed-out. They never once feel too 2-dimensional or undeveloped. <br /><br />I also appreciate the fact that Suze’s stepbrothers are becoming more and more like her family. Doc of course cares about her since the 1st book (I kinda miss him in this book because he’s not present much.) Sleepy/Jake in particular seems to actually care about her well-being. My heart warmed up to see him and Dopey/Brad call her mom their mom too. And she is low-key freaked out about them doing that, but she already seems to be so used to them as her family.<br /><br />And Father Dominic is hilarious and fatherly as always. Love him. Also, it’s interesting to see that he has a backstory, and I hope we get to find out more.<br /><br />Anyway, I think this might be my least favorite of the 3 so far, but I still greatly enjoyed it. I’m going to give this <b>3.5 stars</b>. I just love Suze. Her character is just incredibly funny and relatable. I literally want to be her. Or want to be her best friend. She’s just amazing!<br /><br />Also, side-note but romance is underway but in slow-mo pace. I don’t really mind though because I am focused on the adventures of Suze and the romance seems to be developing naturally.<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ends in a happy enough note but not the last book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Did he make a mistake? When Father Dom learns how to play the Gameboy and gets addicted to it. The ending with the hospital and Gina is there and Jesse materialize when she’s gone. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />---------<br />Here is my weekly Sunday-Mediator-reading for a dose of coziness and humor &lt;3</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7905426154088446066">I normally don’t like pop culture references in books but I love that I get all of the late 90s / early 2000s references this series makes. It definitely dates the books and I’m sure that new younger readers wouldn’t enjoy it but I’m just having so much fun retreading these books. This installment had good moments but it definitely wasn’t my favorite - the plot kind of felt recycled from the other two books? The concept was slightly more compelling than the last book but it also wasn’t too new. </span>
  <span id="freeText7905426154088446066" style="display:none">I normally don’t like pop culture references in books but I love that I get all of the late 90s / early 2000s references this series makes. It definitely dates the books and I’m sure that new younger readers wouldn’t enjoy it but I’m just having so much fun retreading these books. This installment had good moments but it definitely wasn’t my favorite - the plot kind of felt recycled from the other two books? The concept was slightly more compelling than the last book but it also wasn’t too new. These books definitely aren’t earth shattering but they are so much fun! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13990047837703085530"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Even though this is probably the most underwhelming part of the series, I would like to symbolically dedicate my <b>600th review</b> on Goodreads to Meg Cabot. Meg Cabot is the author who absolutely played a huge part of my elementary and high school days and even though her books may not be masterpieces, they made me overcome a lot of problems and made me feel good when I was down. The Mediator series is fast-paced, action-packed and swoon-worthy and I loved both Suze and Jesse. I've always b</span>
  <span id="freeText13990047837703085530" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Even though this is probably the most underwhelming part of the series, I would like to symbolically dedicate my <b>600th review</b> on Goodreads to Meg Cabot. Meg Cabot is the author who absolutely played a huge part of my elementary and high school days and even though her books may not be masterpieces, they made me overcome a lot of problems and made me feel good when I was down. The Mediator series is fast-paced, action-packed and swoon-worthy and I loved both Suze and Jesse. I've always been putting off writing reviews for this series as I don't know what to say except that I formed a huge bond with it and that I often gladly reread some parts of it.<br><br>Anyway, 600th review! Can't believe my little fingers wrote this many reviews on here. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475903796ra/20780511.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To 600 more!</span>

  <span id="freeText14519856639103243986" style="display:none">The story starts with Suze’s best friend from New York coming to visit her in Carmel, California. Suze's stepbrothers Brad and Jake (aka Dopey and Sleepy) suddenly start fighting over Gina's (Suze's friend from New York) attentions. Gina and Suze were hanging at the beach and decide to go get more drinks because it was warm. At the market, something catches Suze's attention, four people in formal wear. Upon further inspection, she notices something else, they are all dead or otherwise known as ghosts. Suze finds that they were called the RLS Angels because they were all brilliant and leaders.<br /><br />Suze learns in one of her classes that it was Michael Meducci who had accidentally rammed the Angels. The Angels are furious at Michael for killing them so they will not stop at anything to kill him. One problem though is that Michael thinks Suze is in love with him so he tries to pursue a relationship with her. The Angels go after Michael but Suze is usually there.<br /><br />Father Dominic and Suze investigate the scene of the accident. Jesse tags along while at home Gina is covering for Suze. Jesse is able to calm the Angels down so that Father Dominic and Suze can talk to them. Suze discovers the truth that Michael killed the RLS Angels on purpose to get revenge on them because his is sister in a coma after drinking too much and almost drowning at a party at one of the Angels’ house. Suze tricks Michael and he confesses but realizes Suze is going to expose him for what he did and he tries to kill Suze. Suze summons the RLS Angels saying the okay to kill Michael but see's she made a mistake and tries to call it off but the Angels are furious. The Angels go after Jesse (who was watching the Angels) and Suze. When the ambulance came Suze is pretty beat up and taken to the hospital after finding out Michael confessed to the police and is going behind bars.<br /><br />The day after Michael’s arrest, her sister woke up from her coma. Everyone visited her except Jesse, which made her sad. Suze caught Jesse trying to dematerialize and felt hurt by that. Her grounding for going with Michael will not start until Gina leaves so it ends that her tests turned back to normal and she can leave the hospital.</span>

  <span id="freeText6492612253066084003" style="display:none">Actual review rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br />Mean Spirits, the third book in the Mediator series was extremely underwhelming. <br /><br />We follow Suzie while she tries to control the spirits that are causing havoc in her new home. She also must keep her secret hidden from her best friend Gina who is visiting from New York. <br /><br />While Gina was a spunky character I didn't feel like she added anything to this story. I felt like she was put in place to put a rift between the other characters in this story and Suzie. For example, she cannot see Jesse because Suzie and Gina are sharing a room and Suzie avoids her brothers because they are all over Gina.<br /><br />I did like The Angels and thought it was interesting that they were so bitter by their deaths. When Suzie was nearly drowned by them it was highly entertaining and I was suprised by how far they took their fight. <br /><br />The ending was a little abrupt and I wish Jesse and Suzie would just get together already! I need more of a romantic storyline in these books. <br /><br />*crappy review as I need to sleep! Might edited in the morning.*</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=school-year-2014-2015">school-year-2014-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998620549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7002646252799545636">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>This is a very fun series and I very much enjoy reading them! These books are beginning to get darker, but they still have the light-hearted moments. <br/><br/>At the store on day, Suze sees four ghosts of teenagers. It turns out that they were the RLS Angels, the most popular kids of RLS and died in a terrible accident the previous weekend. When the Angels keep trying to kill one of her classmates, the class geek by the name of Micha</span>
  <span id="freeText7002646252799545636" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />This is a very fun series and I very much enjoy reading them! These books are beginning to get darker, but they still have the light-hearted moments. <br /><br />At the store on day, Suze sees four ghosts of teenagers. It turns out that they were the RLS Angels, the most popular kids of RLS and died in a terrible accident the previous weekend. When the Angels keep trying to kill one of her classmates, the class geek by the name of Michael, Suze has to get close to Michael. As it turns out, Michael was the other driver in the accident and came out unscaved and the Angels want revenge, but what really happened that night?<br /><br />Each book in this series focuses on a different ghostly encounter, which I very much like. The whole idea of a girl seeing ghosts isn't really something I haven't seen before, but I still like these books. The whole outlook in this series is more light-hearted, more for younger audiences, which is refreshing. Though, the mysteries in this books are getting more and more dark and I actually really like that! <br /><br />I did like the mystery in this book involving the Angels. It was a bit predictable, at points, but I did like trying to figure it all out!<br /><br />As for romance, there isn't really any *frowns*<br />But, ship ship ship ship SHIP!<br />I admit, that my favorite part of this series is just shipping Suze and Jesse. Though, there is some more development with them, so there's that.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />Overall, a great addition to the series! I am definitely planning on reading more, in fact, I just finished reading the next book! If you want a fun, ghostly series, this is a great series to read!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875992086" />
    <a title="Aylee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4511060-aylee"><img alt="Aylee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294094939p2/4511060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875992086?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aylee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aylee" href="/user/show/4511060-aylee">Aylee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875992086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer745556548849057949"><a href='http://recoveringpotteraddict.blogspot.ca/2017/02/series-review-mediator-by-meg-cabot.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>You can also read this review on my blog.</a><br/><br/>This review applies to the entire Mediator Series.<br/><br/><br/>The Mediator Series was my first series read of the year and let me tell you, it was a fantastically FUN way to start off my reading year. The series follows Suze Simon who has the ability to see, to talk to, and to beat up - whatever the occasion warrants - ghosts in order to send them on their way to the afterworld. The series was completed after six books in 2005, with an added novella and seventh novel</span>
  <span id="freeText745556548849057949" style="display:none"><a href="http://recoveringpotteraddict.blogspot.ca/2017/02/series-review-mediator-by-meg-cabot.html" rel="nofollow noopener">You can also read this review on my blog.</a><br /><br />This review applies to the entire Mediator Series.<br /><br /><br />The Mediator Series was my first series read of the year and let me tell you, it was a fantastically FUN way to start off my reading year. The series follows Suze Simon who has the ability to see, to talk to, and to beat up - whatever the occasion warrants - ghosts in order to send them on their way to the afterworld. The series was completed after six books in 2005, with an added novella and seventh novel set a decade later in 2016.<br /><br />Suze Simon is definitely the best part of the series for me. I would want to be BFFs with her if not for the fact that I am convinced that she is WAY too cool for me. This girl has more personality in her pinkie finger than most protagonists have developed over the course of an entire book. Suze's singular sass, nerve, and fashion sense put her right up there with The Greats Buffy Summers and Veronica Mars, in my mind. In fact, the Mediator Series reads a lot like those teen serialized TV shows set in small town California that follow a new story each episode, in addition to being easy entertainment to take in.<br /><br />This is my first Meg Cabot read - can you believe it? And if all of her protagonists are as fun as Suze Simon, then I am looking forward to reading more from her. I'm curious, which are the Meg Cabot books that I absolutely must read next? I would love recommendations!</span>
  <a data-text-id="745556548849057949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10308593793385412251">I'm not much of a YA fan anymore and it's been years since I read the previous books of the series, so I was hesitant picking this one up, but I'm glad I finally did.<br/><br/>Suze, the teenage mediator, reluctantly gets involved with a group of ghosts that seem to be out for revenge. She is more of the hit now, get answers later kind of girl, but thankfully her allies, the principal of her school who is also a mediator, and Jesse, the ghost boy that shares her room, are there to provide alternative solut</span>
  <span id="freeText10308593793385412251" style="display:none">I'm not much of a YA fan anymore and it's been years since I read the previous books of the series, so I was hesitant picking this one up, but I'm glad I finally did.<br /><br />Suze, the teenage mediator, reluctantly gets involved with a group of ghosts that seem to be out for revenge. She is more of the hit now, get answers later kind of girl, but thankfully her allies, the principal of her school who is also a mediator, and Jesse, the ghost boy that shares her room, are there to provide alternative solutions.<br /><br />Suze soon realizes that their target is one of her classmates, and she does her best to make sure they don't succeed in killing him, having him get attached to her for her efforts. In the end it turns out that the ghosts did not become so because of a car accident, as people believed, but were purposefully run off the street instead by the boy, who wanted to get revenge on them for his sister's coma after she nearly drowned in one of their parties.<br /><br />A light story, despite the dark theme, that leaves Suze <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in the hospital, after the latest of many near death experiences <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but a little bit wiser than before. Her story continues in the short story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15989191.Every_Girl_s_Dream__The_Mediator___3_5_" title="Every Girl's Dream (The Mediator, #3.5) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Girl's Dream</a>.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73375761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5121177568630562381">This is my favorite in the series so far (I know it just keeps getting better and better) but I LOVED Reunion. The RLS Angels were my favorite ghosts so far (Jesse excluded), and I loved that Jake, Brad, and David had become Suze's family and she was very protective of them (and them of her). Their relationships have just strengthened with each book--with the occasional tryst as with all siblings. <br/><br/>I sort of laughed that Gina came out to visit her best friend but they spent little time together. </span>
  <span id="freeText5121177568630562381" style="display:none">This is my favorite in the series so far (I know it just keeps getting better and better) but I LOVED Reunion. The RLS Angels were my favorite ghosts so far (Jesse excluded), and I loved that Jake, Brad, and David had become Suze's family and she was very protective of them (and them of her). Their relationships have just strengthened with each book--with the occasional tryst as with all siblings. <br /><br />I sort of laughed that Gina came out to visit her best friend but they spent little time together. (I'm visiting my cross-country best friend in a few weeks and you know we will be spending every minute together. Gotta take advantage when you're in the same time-zone) HOWEVER, Gina was a great addition to the book. I hope we see more of her throughout the series (I can't remember *FINGERS CROSSED*) Father Dom seemed very naive in Reunion, which I did not appreciate. I always felt like he was very wise and I didn't get that in this one. Nonetheless he is fabulous and a great father-figure for Suze.<br /><br />There were so many high points throughout this book. I know because I loved this book the first time around and remembered a great deal more of this one than the others. All I can say is MORE SUZE AND JESSE IN DARKEST HOUR PLEASE.</span>

<div id="review_350873261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350873261" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10303433-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506476466p2/10303433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350873261?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/10303433-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10303433-megan?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350873261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1632163257550030361">Original rating: 4 stars<br/>7/2020 reread: 4.5 stars<br/><br/>--<blockquote>
  <i>One thing I have to admit about the ocean: It's very quiet down there. I mean, really. No more shrieking gulls, crashing of the waves, shouts from the surfers. No, under the sea, it's just you and the water and the ghosts who are trying to kill you.</i>
</blockquote><b>Reunion</b> was the best installment of <b>The Mediator</b> series yet. The inclusion of Gina, Suze's best friend from New York, is greatly appreciated. Suze feels markedly more confident and at ease in scene</span>
  <span id="freeText1632163257550030361" style="display:none">Original rating: 4 stars<br />7/2020 reread: 4.5 stars<br /><br />--<blockquote>
  <i>One thing I have to admit about the ocean: It's very quiet down there. I mean, really. No more shrieking gulls, crashing of the waves, shouts from the surfers. No, under the sea, it's just you and the water and the ghosts who are trying to kill you.</i>
</blockquote><b>Reunion</b> was the best installment of <b>The Mediator</b> series yet. The inclusion of Gina, Suze's best friend from New York, is greatly appreciated. Suze feels markedly more confident and at ease in scenes with Gina, whose sharp yet laid-back personality really complemented Suze's more chaotic nature. The opening chapters of the book, which introduce the reader to both Gina and the ghost(s) of the week, are delightfully tight, with a perfect, sassy tone that I just loved. The scene in Jimmy's mart where Suze raises her sunglasses to stare at the four teenage ghosts attempting to lift some beer was so effortlessly on-point.<br /><br />Again, the plot of the book is deceptively dark. The current mystery features the tragic deaths of the "RLS Angels," four ultra-popular, beautiful, and promising seniors from a rival high school. The Angels plunged to their death after an "accidental" automobile collision on a narrow cliff-side road. Only, of course, there's nothing accidental about it. Suze soon discovers that book three's faux-LI (and the other driver in the collision that killed the Angels), Michael Meducci, may not be telling the full truth about his involvement in the crash.<br /><br />What we discover, of course, is that<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Michael <b>did</b> kill the Angels in cold blood. Yet Michael's motivations are heartbreakingly understandable when it's revealed that the so-called "stars" of the local community had facilitated the near-death of his twelve-year-old sister:<blockquote><i>"That's what one of the EMS guys told the police. Everybody thought she was faking it." He let out a humorless laugh. "My sister--that was all she wanted, you know? To be popular. To be like them. And they stood there. They all just stood there laughing while she drowned."</i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Like damn. I dunno about you, but that's some real shit. <br /><br />Pair this with the improvement in writing and characterization (I really do think Suze's character became fully defined in this volume), and you get quite the enjoyable read, in my humble opinion. There were so many legitimately funny, incisive scenes in this book that I honestly lost track of how many quotes tickled my fancy. It was so fun. <br /><br />Of course, you know I gotta talk a bit about the Jesse x Suze. Their dynamic here is so special, honestly. They've reached a point of genuine friendship and <i>warmth</i>, which is just never not incredible to read. They trust and rely on one another, and they truly love to simply be in one another's company:<blockquote>
  <i>"I don't understand why you are so unhappy about it," Jesse said. He had stretched out across the tiles, contented as I'd ever seen him. "I like it much better this way."<br />"What way?" I groused. I couldn't get quite as comfortable. I kept finding prickly pine needles beneath my butt.<br />"Just the two of us," he said with a shrug. "Like it's always been."</i>
</blockquote>Haaaaaa….fucking kill me, I love them so much. <br /><br />Anyways, I'm already well into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23224.Darkest_Hour__The_Mediator___4_" title="Darkest Hour (The Mediator, #4) by Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkest Hour</a>, so my feels are a bit preoccupied right at this moment. I'll wrap this up and spare my key smashing for the nonsense that is about to occur.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1632163257550030361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1392104066" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392104066" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392104066?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392104066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15069519640985984199">2020 Reread: This is really where the series picks up steam. I really like Gina and Sleepy (I vaguely remember having them as a ship in the Paul/Suze fan fic I wrote way back in the day-I know blasphemy but I always preferred Saul in fan fic to Juze which is the opposite to cannon) anyway old fan fics aside and back to 2020 reflections. I didn't really struggle or get bored with this book like I did with one and two. Not that one and two are particularly bad by any means, the plot is just not ne</span>
  <span id="freeText15069519640985984199" style="display:none">2020 Reread: This is really where the series picks up steam. I really like Gina and Sleepy (I vaguely remember having them as a ship in the Paul/Suze fan fic I wrote way back in the day-I know blasphemy but I always preferred Saul in fan fic to Juze which is the opposite to cannon) anyway old fan fics aside and back to 2020 reflections. I didn't really struggle or get bored with this book like I did with one and two. Not that one and two are particularly bad by any means, the plot is just not nearly as strong there's really a lot of overlap with the Thad and Bryce characters and honestly they are more introduction-ish than anything else. <br /><br />Really 3.5 stars to see review with shirtless Thor gif click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/10/02/sleepy-and-gina-for-the-win-reunion-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />What I Remember:<br /><br />When I first read this I was sort of in a rush, but there were a few things that stuck out. One being the relationship between Suze’s NYC bestie, Gina, and her stepbrother, Sleepy. I shipped them oddly enough and they were a background relationship. Also, I loved the action scenes in this book. Although, this isn’t the zenith of action for this series (that alone goes to book four), this one does have a few good ghost busting moments. And I was entranced enough to get through it without my eyes wondering to the last book.<br /><br />Reread:<br /><br />Reunion holds up pretty well, but it is a filler book. It really isn’t until the fourth book in this series that things start moving for the overall series arc.<br /><br />Although, there is more Suze and Jesse development. So, yay on that front.<br /><br />To be honest, books 1-3 follow a similar format. Suze attracts the eye of a guy who is somehow being haunted or knows someone who’s being haunted.<br /><br />In this book it’s Michael Meducci who I always view as Michael Moscovtiz evil twin who is less sexy but probably just as nerdy that ends up killing Josh Ritcher.<br /><br />Okay, that didn’t happen in The Princess Diaries. Though, it could’ve if Meg Cabot wanted to sort of make in like The Heathers.<br /><br />Weird digression aside, it’s interesting in this book that the hot guy Suze has to watch over isn’t really that hot-unless he’s not wearing any clothes. And is borderline creepy.<br /><br />Another bonus to this book, was the introduction of Gina. Who is one of my favorite side characters. And I really did like the side ship with her and Sleepy. She’s the reason I tolerate that stepbrother. I like Doc too. Never really grew to like Dopey though, but I think that’s the typical feeling.<br /><br />Anyway, Gina has some great lines in this installment. Some of my favorite, involved her reacting to Kelly Prescott’s proposed tank policy against China. Why I find it hilarious, upon reread is the ridiculous election that’s going on in the US right now. Seriously, I felt that every ludicrous thing Kelly Prescott said was akin to something The Donald would say.<br /><br />As far as filler books go, I found this one a little bit more tolerable than Ninth Key not that Ninth Key is bad, it’s just definite filler.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15069519640985984199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1156401003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156401003" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38661143-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473203271p2/38661143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156401003?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/38661143-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38661143-k?shelf=cabot-the-mediator-series">cabot-the-mediator-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38661143-k?shelf=_au-meg-cabot">_au-meg-cabot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156401003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6424641562670555652"><i> Reunion </i> is only the third book of "The Mediator" series, and despite having read only the two prequels to this, I know for a fact that this <i> is </i> and <i> will be </i>my all-time favorite book of the series. <i> Shadowland </i> and <i> Ninth Key </i> were amazing, too, trust me, but I've always enjoyed a good murder mystery. And this happened to be one. <br/><br/>Whenever I read a book, I try to finish it in one sitting. It's much more satisfying and <i> thrilling </i> for me to escape into an alternate universe for an extended peri</span>
  <span id="freeText6424641562670555652" style="display:none"><i> Reunion </i> is only the third book of "The Mediator" series, and despite having read only the two prequels to this, I know for a fact that this <i> is </i> and <i> will be </i>my all-time favorite book of the series. <i> Shadowland </i> and <i> Ninth Key </i> were amazing, too, trust me, but I've always enjoyed a good murder mystery. And this happened to be one. <br /><br />Whenever I read a book, I try to finish it in one sitting. It's much more satisfying and <i> thrilling </i> for me to escape into an alternate universe for an extended period of time without constantly being disrupted by trivial things such as putting the groceries away or even eating. I was lucky enough that I was able to read this 304-paged and rather fast-paced yet unfailingly witty and captivating story in a somewhat continuous stretch of five hours. <br /><br />The plot instantly sucked me in the second I realized that Gina, Suze's best friend from New York, was visiting during her spring break. She isn't a frequently-mentioned character in the previous two books, however Gina does know a little bit about her friend's mediation abilities. I was anticipating how Suze would try to keep her normal, non-mediator friend from getting involved in all the ghost chaos. Because in this book, there isn't just one ghost but <i> four</i>. <br /><br />They're a group of friends: two popular couples from a rivaling school. They were tragically killed when their car toppled over a cliff. Only it wasn't just a car accident that everybody suspects it to be. Their murderer is still alive and innocent in the eyes of the public. Suze decides to take matters in her own hands when her family is threatened, but like always, nothing ever goes the way she plans. <br /><br />Meg Cabot, once again, stunned me with her extremely well-written, engaging and thrilling mystery. I love the details she gives to all of her characters. I never saw the twists coming and I spent half the time second-guessing each character. I'm sad to see that the book is over, and while I'm looking forward to the next installment of the series, I do wish I hadn't reached the end of this story so quickly. This was, by far, the best book in the lot. <br /><br />5 out of 5 stars; mainly for such a creative plot (Hooray for murder mysteries!), the characterization, the complete <i> anticipation </i> I was literally feeling throughout reading, the language (I loved Suze's innocent oblivion and the way she takes quite a while to figure things out) and sarcasm, and just for being awesome book overall. I wish I could dock off a point because there weren't nearly enough satisfactory interactions between Suze and Jesse (I'm just as frustrated as Suze is!)... but I'll try to be fair. Until the "Darkest Hour"!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6424641562670555652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13773537816062642952" style="display:none"><b>This is like a fangirling mess, so read at your own caution</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The adventures of Suze continue! I really loved having Gina come visit. She's also one of the few people who know about Suze's ghostly business and she actually gets to learn a bit more about it. Whenever I read books were the main character moves I feel like we never really get much from their past friendships, it's just like oh well I moved must cease contact. We got more interaction with Suze's stepbrothers because of them vying for Gina's affections. Out of the three brothers I always feel like Jake is the one I know less about cause he's always working or sleeping (hence the nickname Sleepy) but him and Gina have a little thing so he's more active and talkative in this book.<br /><br />Speaking of Suze's stepbrothers, their casual use of the word "mom" in this book just throws Suze for a loop every time it's mentioned. She's just like <i>whoa, wait, when did they start referring to my mom as just mom in reference to them</i>. I like that that shows how they've really kinda accepted their new family status. They have no problem with it. And, ya know, Brad and Suze already fight like brother and sister. Suze took quickest to David cause he's younger and adorable. And Jake's basically been acting like big brother since he went to her aid at the end of book one, I really love when he plays big brother like in this book.<br /><br />And as usual there's always some Suze/Jesse moments that make me squeal with glee. This interaction especially:<br /><b><i>"I don't understand why you are so unhappy about it," Jesse said. He had stretched out across the tiles, contented as I'd ever seen him. "I like it much better this way."<br />"What way?" I groused. I couldn't get quite as comfortable. I kept finding prickly pine needles beneath my butt.<br />"Just the two of us," he said with a shrug. "Like it's always been."</i></b><br />JUST THE TWO OF US!! HE LIKES HIS ALONE TIME WITH YOU SUSANNAH!<br /><br />I think my favorite scene from the book though is when Suze, Jesse, and Father D go down to the beach where the RLS Angels died and talk to them. I liked the trek down there and all the different interactions that went on. And then getting the whole story about how they died. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Book Status Section:<br />pg. 124: Yes, woo the girl by taking her to the scene of the crime<br />pg. 124 again: OMG PLEASE MICHAEL (in reference to him talking about the make out point<br />pg. 124 yet again: LOOOOOLLLLLL Suze couldn't get out of that car fast enough!<br />pg. 212: I always imagine Suze rolling her eyes after talking to Michael<br />pg. 214: Jake being all big brotherly :)</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13773537816062642952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153271336" />
    <a title="Reading Vacation" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation"><img alt="Reading Vacation" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341857406p2/5102733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153271336?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Vacation" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Vacation" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation">Reading Vacation</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153271336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer434116986899746206">REVIEW<br/><br/>A triple decker review. This is what you end up with when a series is so good that you read the books one right after the other. <br/><br/>In Ninth Key, Suze spends a good part of her time trying to figure out if Tad Beaumont (aka Red) is responsible for a murder. While the interactions between Suze and Tad were nice, I was much more drawn to the scenes with Suze and Jesse. Remember Jesse, he’s the ghost who lives in Suze’s room. Less Red and more Jesse! There are some completely unexpected twists t</span>
  <span id="freeText434116986899746206" style="display:none">REVIEW<br /><br />A triple decker review. This is what you end up with when a series is so good that you read the books one right after the other. <br /><br />In Ninth Key, Suze spends a good part of her time trying to figure out if Tad Beaumont (aka Red) is responsible for a murder. While the interactions between Suze and Tad were nice, I was much more drawn to the scenes with Suze and Jesse. Remember Jesse, he’s the ghost who lives in Suze’s room. Less Red and more Jesse! There are some completely unexpected twists to the plot and I LOVED the way Meg Cabot worked them in. She is a genius at writing a mystery. GENIUS.<br /><br />Reunion is my favorite Mediator book of the series so far. In this book, Suze is caught between the ghosts of four teens who died in a car accident (the RLS Angels) and Michael, the boy from her school who the ghosts are blaming for their deaths. It’s an all-out war as the ghosts are trying to get revenge on Michael. There is no shortage of action and I liked that the car accident plot was so realistic. Even with ghosts being involved, the plot felt very REAL.<br /><br />In Darkest Hour, Suze comes face-to-face with Maria, the ghost who was engaged to her beloved Jesse. Since I am so into the relationship between Suze and Jesse, I was really excited to read about Jesse’s former fiancé. The most romantic of the series so far, Darkest Hour will tug at your heart. Be prepared for a little side-plot action with the little boy Suze is babysitting – his name is Jack and he’s an eight-year-old mediator. I really enjoy how Meg Cabot put awesome little gems like this into her stories. <br /><br />It’s easy to see that I love the Mediator series. I can’t wait to read Haunted (book 5) and Twilight (book 6). <br /><br />RATING<br /><br />5 Plot<br /><br />4 Characters<br /><br />5 Attention Grabbing<br /><br />5 Girlie Meter<br /><br />4 Ending<br /><br /><br />23 TOTAL<br /><br /><br />5 STARS</span>
  <a data-text-id="434116986899746206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_366119283" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/366119283" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1979147-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/366119283?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1979147-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1979147-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer366119283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15957945208448748361">The third book in the Mediator series, Reunion, was significantly weaker than the first two. After loving the second book in the series, Ninth Key, I was thoroughly disappointed by this one for two main reasons: the setting and the characters. <br/><br/>Cabot started out strong in the first two books, but she lost is me on the setting in this one. Living in Northern California I can definitively state that nobody sane could wear a bikini on a beach in March. Yes, it might be over 70 degrees, but that wind</span>
  <span id="freeText15957945208448748361" style="display:none">The third book in the Mediator series, Reunion, was significantly weaker than the first two. After loving the second book in the series, Ninth Key, I was thoroughly disappointed by this one for two main reasons: the setting and the characters. <br /><br />Cabot started out strong in the first two books, but she lost is me on the setting in this one. Living in Northern California I can definitively state that nobody sane could wear a bikini on a beach in March. Yes, it might be over 70 degrees, but that wind is <i>cold</i>. Even in July the wind strongly encourages you to put on a sweatshirt. I'm also fairly certain there is no indoor mall in Carmel - and there is definitely not a Chick-Fil-A. So that scene would have taken place at an outdoor mall, which doesn't work so well because those don't really have ceilings from which to hang large decorative objects. <br /><br />Secondly, the characters - the antagonist was not a believable character at all. I also felt that he perpetuated negative stereotypes of the 'geek' or 'nerd' which is really not a great thing for our society. This character is truly key to the plot, and so this weaknesses is what led to the book's failure. I was happy to see Suze and Father Dom bond more in this book, and she finally asked for his help! However, I feel that Cabot is still trying to figure out Father Dom's character which is a bit frustrating. The character development of Suze's brothers was fantastic, but left me wondering why the mom is rarely in the story. <br /><br />I am very curious to see where Cabot goes with the rest of this series! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15957945208448748361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library"><img alt="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586826564p2/6095877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lubnaa (Romance Library)" href="/user/show/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library">Lubnaa (Romance Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=interracial-couples">interracial-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6095877-lubnaa-romance-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241692006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5465164089431280962"><b>Re-read in 2020 on audio:</b><br/><br/>Reunion is the third book in the Mediator series and this time around, Suze has to protect one of her classmates from a group of vengeful teenage ghosts. This book is definitely darker than the previous two books and things get pretty personal for Suze. The climax actually gave me goosebumps. The plot surrounding the vengeful teenage ghosts paves the way for some awesome character and relationship development. First, I love seeing Father Dom, Suze, and Jesse working toge</span>
  <span id="freeText5465164089431280962" style="display:none"><b>Re-read in 2020 on audio:</b><br /><br />Reunion is the third book in the Mediator series and this time around, Suze has to protect one of her classmates from a group of vengeful teenage ghosts. This book is definitely darker than the previous two books and things get pretty personal for Suze. The climax actually gave me goosebumps. The plot surrounding the vengeful teenage ghosts paves the way for some awesome character and relationship development. First, I love seeing Father Dom, Suze, and Jesse working together! Furthermore, Suze finally realizes that Sleepy, Dopey, and Dock are...you know...family lol even though she constantly clarifies that they're her "stepbrothers." It was particularly great seeing Sleepy being all brotherly toward Suze. <br /><br />There's also relationship development between Jesse and Suze, with Suze realizing that Jesse might be her fated one true love, as predicted by the psychic. Jesse...well, we kind of see him being riled up and affected by the events in this book, but his feelings are still not 100% clear to Suze. And this works because Jesse's backstory will finally take the spotlight in the next book! As far as I remember, the second half of the series is where shit actually gets real. So excited to find out more about Jesse, whose story I only remember in bits and pieces. And...Paul is also coming up soon LOL.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5465164089431280962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QrLUluKunbSTiq1bXqbWMAajWESMwzNmCttTuxm7UnXU2aFhB43SNt2zkT9TgDpAmcpEFltvBuzABpRDSUCBWg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('em1+viOVdzd/etGWI+APUZZW/C5XVOcH/RilqsOL2PLsBgtJxrY4tTFD7fIuxuMhCT/gfID40o03xWJSk3AL3Q==')})
  }
